       1                 :            : /* -----------------------------------------------------------------------
       2                 :            :  * formatting.c
       3                 :            :  *
       4                 :            :  * $PostgreSQL: pgsql/src/backend/utils/adt/formatting.c,v 1.137.2.2 2009/07/06 19:11:53 heikki Exp $
       5                 :            :  *
       6                 :            :  *
       7                 :            :  *       Portions Copyright (c) 1999-2008, PostgreSQL Global Development Group
       8                 :            :  *
       9                 :            :  *
      10                 :            :  *       TO_CHAR(); TO_TIMESTAMP(); TO_DATE(); TO_NUMBER();
      11                 :            :  *
      12                 :            :  *       The PostgreSQL routines for a timestamp/int/float/numeric formatting,
      13                 :            :  *       inspired by the Oracle TO_CHAR() / TO_DATE() / TO_NUMBER() routines.
      14                 :            :  *
      15                 :            :  *
      16                 :            :  *       Cache & Memory:
      17                 :            :  *      Routines use (itself) internal cache for format pictures.
      18                 :            :  *
      19                 :            :  *      The cache uses a static buffer and is persistent across transactions.  If
      20                 :            :  *      the format-picture is bigger than the cache buffer, the parser is called
      21                 :            :  *      always.
      22                 :            :  *
      23                 :            :  *       NOTE for Number version:
      24                 :            :  *      All in this version is implemented as keywords ( => not used
      25                 :            :  *      suffixes), because a format picture is for *one* item (number)
      26                 :            :  *      only. It not is as a timestamp version, where each keyword (can)
      27                 :            :  *      has suffix.
      28                 :            :  *
      29                 :            :  *       NOTE for Timestamp routines:
      30                 :            :  *      In this module the POSIX 'struct tm' type is *not* used, but rather
      31                 :            :  *      PgSQL type, which has tm_mon based on one (*non* zero) and
      32                 :            :  *      year *not* based on 1900, but is used full year number.
      33                 :            :  *      Module supports AD / BC / AM / PM.
      34                 :            :  *
      35                 :            :  *      Supported types for to_char():
      36                 :            :  *
      37                 :            :  *              Timestamp, Numeric, int4, int8, float4, float8
      38                 :            :  *
      39                 :            :  *      Supported types for reverse conversion:
      40                 :            :  *
      41                 :            :  *              Timestamp       - to_timestamp()
      42                 :            :  *              Date            - to_date()
      43                 :            :  *              Numeric         - to_number()
      44                 :            :  *
      45                 :            :  *
      46                 :            :  *      Karel Zak
      47                 :            :  *
      48                 :            :  * TODO
      49                 :            :  *      - better number building (formatting) / parsing, now it isn't
      50                 :            :  *                ideal code
      51                 :            :  *      - use Assert()
      52                 :            :  *      - add support for abstime
      53                 :            :  *      - add support for roman number to standard number conversion
      54                 :            :  *      - add support for number spelling
      55                 :            :  *      - add support for string to string formatting (we must be better
      56                 :            :  *        than Oracle :-),
      57                 :            :  *              to_char('Hello', 'X X X X X') -> 'H e l l o'
      58                 :            :  *
      59                 :            :  * -----------------------------------------------------------------------
      60                 :            :  */
      61                 :            : 
      62                 :            : #ifdef DEBUG_TO_FROM_CHAR
      63                 :            : #define DEBUG_elog_output       DEBUG3

     473                 :            :         (_X)->tm_sec  = (_X)->tm_year = (_X)->tm_min = (_X)->tm_wday = \
     474                 :            :         (_X)->tm_hour = (_X)->tm_yday = (_X)->tm_isdst = 0; \
     475                 :            :         (_X)->tm_mday = (_X)->tm_mon  = 1; \
     476                 :            : } while(0)
     477                 :            : 
     478                 :            : #define ZERO_tmtc(_X) \
     479                 :            : do { \
     480                 :            :         ZERO_tm( tmtcTm(_X) ); \
     481                 :            :         tmtcFsec(_X) = 0; \
     482                 :            :         tmtcTzn(_X) = NULL; \
     483                 :            : } while(0)
     484                 :            : 
     485                 :            : /*
     486                 :            :  *      to_char(time) appears to to_char() as an interval, so this check
     487                 :            :  *      is really for interval and time data types.
     488                 :            :  */
     489                 :            : #define INVALID_FOR_INTERVAL  \
     490                 :            : do { \
     491                 :            :         if (is_interval) \
     492                 :            :                 ereport(ERROR, \
     493                 :            :                                 (errcode(ERRCODE_INVALID_DATETIME_FORMAT), \
     494                 :            :                                  errmsg("invalid format specification for an interval value"), \
     495                 :            :                                  errhint("Intervals are not tied to specific calendar dates."))); \
     496                 :            : } while(0)

     542                 :            : 
     543                 :            : /* ----------
     544                 :            :  * Format-pictures (KeyWord).
     545                 :            :  *
     546                 :            :  * The KeyWord field; alphabetic sorted, *BUT* strings alike is sorted
     547                 :            :  *                complicated -to-> easy:
     548                 :            :  *
     549                 :            :  *      (example: "DDD","DD","Day","D" )
     550                 :            :  *
     551                 :            :  * (this specific sort needs the algorithm for sequential search for strings,
     552                 :            :  * which not has exact end; -> How keyword is in "HH12blabla" ? - "HH"
     553                 :            :  * or "HH12"? You must first try "HH12", because "HH" is in string, but
     554                 :            :  * it is not good.
     555                 :            :  *
     556                 :            :  * (!)
     557                 :            :  *       - Position for the keyword is similar as position in the enum DCH/NUM_poz.
     558                 :            :  * (!)
     559                 :            :  *
     560                 :            :  * For fast search is used the 'int index[]', index is ascii table from position
     561                 :            :  * 32 (' ') to 126 (~), in this index is DCH_ / NUM_ enums for each ASCII
     562                 :            :  * position or -1 if char is not used in the KeyWord. Search example for
     563                 :            :  * string "MM":
     564                 :            :  *      1)      see in index to index['M' - 32],
     565                 :            :  *      2)      take keywords position (enum DCH_MI) from index
     566                 :            :  *      3)      run sequential search in keywords[] from this position
     567                 :            :  *
     568                 :            :  * ----------
     569                 :            :  */
     570                 :            :
